================================================================================
FILE: backend\api\routes.py

   1: """
   2: routes.py — FastAPI route definitions for the Smart Grid API.
   3: 
   4: Uses FastAPI dependency injection (Request → app.state) instead of
   5: mutable module-level globals, which eliminates NoneType type errors.
   6: """
   7: 
   8: from __future__ import annotations
   9: 
  10: import threading
  11: from typing import Optional, TYPE_CHECKING
  12: from fastapi import APIRouter, HTTPException, Request  # type: ignore
  13: from pydantic import BaseModel  # type: ignore
  14: 
  15: from simulation.grid import SmartGrid  # type: ignore
  16: from simulation.scada import ScadaControlCenter  # type: ignore
  17: from simulation.ems import EnergyManagementSystem  # type: ignore
  18: from models.rl_agent import ACTIONS, N_ACTIONS  # type: ignore
  19: 
  20: if TYPE_CHECKING:
  21:     from models.lstm_model import DemandForecaster  # type: ignore
  22:     from models.fault_detector import FaultDetector  # type: ignore
  23: 
  24: router = APIRouter()
  25: grid_lock = threading.Lock()
  26: 
  27: 
  28: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  29: # Dependency helpers — pull singletons from app.state
  30: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  31: 
  32: def get_grid(request: Request) -> SmartGrid:
  33:     return request.app.state.grid
  34: 
  35: 
  36: def get_scada(request: Request) -> ScadaControlCenter:
  37:     return request.app.state.scada
  38: 
  39: 
  40: def get_ems(request: Request) -> EnergyManagementSystem:
  41:     return request.app.state.ems
  42: 
  43: 
  44: def get_forecaster(request: Request):
  45:     return get_scada(request).forecaster
  46: 
  47: 
  48: def get_fault_detector(request: Request):
  49:     return get_scada(request).fault_detector
  50: 
  51: 
  52: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  53: # Helper functions
  54: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  55: 
  56: def _apply_action(action_name: str, state_before: dict, grid: SmartGrid, scada: ScadaControlCenter) -> str:
  57:     """Apply an action using SCADA dispatch logic."""
  58:     return scada._dispatch_control_signal(action_name, state_before, grid)
  59: 
  60: 
  61: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  62: # Request / Response Models
  63: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  64: 
  65: class EventRequest(BaseModel):
  66:     type: str                    # "failure" | "storm" | "clear_storm" | "demand" | "generation" | "restore"
  67:     node_id: Optional[str] = None
  68:     amount: Optional[float] = None
  69: 
  70: 
  71: class ActionRequest(BaseModel):
  72:     action_id: int               # 0–4
  73: 
  74: class NodeRequest(BaseModel):
  75:     type: str                    # "generator" | "substation" | "house"
  76:     position: list[float]        # [x, y]
  77: 
  78: class PositionRequest(BaseModel):
  79:     x: float
  80:     y: float
  81: 
  82: class EdgeRequest(BaseModel):
  83:     source: str
  84:     target: str
  85: 
  86: class NodeTargetRequest(BaseModel):
  87:     node_id: str
  88: 
  89: 
  90: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  91: # GET /health
  92: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  93: 
  94: @router.get("/health")
  95: def health_check() -> dict:
  96:     return {"status": "ok", "message": "Smart Grid API is running"}
  97: 
  98: 
  99: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 100: # GET /state
 101: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 102: 
 103: @router.get("/state")
 104: def get_state(request: Request) -> dict:
 105:     """Return the full current grid state without advancing simulation."""
 106:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 107:     return grid.get_state()
 108: 
 109: 
 110: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 111: # POST /simulate
 112: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 113: 
 114: @router.post("/simulate")
 115: def simulate_step(request: Request) -> dict:
 116:     """
 117:     Advance simulation by 1 timestep.
 118: 
 119:     Real CPS execution order (enforced here):
 120:       1. grid.update_generation()  — Generation (solar + wind + time-based curves)
 121:       2. grid.update_power_flow()  — Physics FIRST (backward/forward sweep)
 122:       3. ems.run(grid)              — EMS reacts to REAL imbalance (storage dispatch)
 123:       4. grid.update_power_flow()  — Recompute after EMS
 124:       5. scada.execute_control_loop() — SCADA AI (fault detection, FLISR rerouting)
 125:       6. grid.update_power_flow()  — Final recompute (after reroute)
 126: 
 127:     EMS runs AFTER physics so it reacts to real imbalance (not pre-empt it).
 128:     EMS uses partial control (50 % absorption) so imbalance remains visible.
 129:     """
 130:     with grid_lock:
 131:         grid:  SmartGrid             = get_grid(request)
 132:         ems:   EnergyManagementSystem = get_ems(request)
 133:         scada: ScadaControlCenter    = get_scada(request)
 134: 
 135:         # ── 1. Generation (solar + wind) ──
 136:         grid.update_generation()
 137: 
 138:         # ── 2. Physics FIRST ──
 139:         grid.update_power_flow()
 140: 
 141:         # ── 3. EMS reacts to REAL imbalance ──
 142:         ems_report = ems.run(grid)
 143: 
 144:         # ── 4. Recompute after EMS ──
 145:         grid.update_power_flow()
 146: 
 147:         # ── 5. SCADA + FLISR ──
 148:         scada_report = scada.execute_control_loop(grid, ems)
 149: 
 150:         # ── 6. Final recompute (after reroute) ──
 151:         grid.update_power_flow()
 152: 
 153:         return {
 154:             "grid": grid.get_state(),
 155:             "ems": {
 156:                 "cycle":            ems_report["cycle"],
 157:                 "balance_mw":       ems_report["balance"],
 158:                 "total_gen":        ems_report["total_gen"],
 159:                 "total_load":       ems_report["total_load"],
 160:                 "absorption_ratio": ems_report["absorption_ratio"],
 161:                 "log":              ems_report["log"],
 162:                 "message":          ems_report["message"],
 163:             },
 164:             "ai": {
 165:                 "predicted_load":     scada_report["predicted_load"],
 166:                 "decision":           scada_report["decision"],
 167:                 "action_result":      scada_report["action_result"],
 168:                 "flisr_log":          scada_report.get("flisr_log", []),
 169:                 "fault_analysis":     scada_report["fault_analysis"],
 170:                 "cycle_id":           scada_report["cycle_id"],
 171:                 "timestamp":          scada_report["timestamp"],
 172:                 "hour_of_day":        scada_report["hour_of_day"],
 173:                 "control_divergence": scada_report["control_divergence"],
 174:                 "overload_warnings":  scada_report.get("overload_warnings", []),
 175:             },
 176:         }
 177: 
 178: 
 179: 
 180: 
 181: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 182: # Grid Construction APIs (User Controlled)
 183: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 184: 
 185: @router.post("/add_node")
 186: def add_user_node(req: NodeRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 187:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 188:     try:
 189:         x, y = req.position[0], req.position[1]
 190:         nid = grid.add_user_node(req.type, x, y)
 191:         return {"message": f"Added node: {nid['id']}", "grid": grid.get_state()}
 192:     except ValueError as e:
 193:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=str(e))
 194: 
 195: @router.put("/nodes/{node_id}/move")
 196: def move_user_node(node_id: str, req: PositionRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 197:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 198:     try:
 199:         grid.move_node(node_id, req.x, req.y)
 200:         return {"message": f"Moved {node_id}", "grid": grid.get_state()}
 201:     except ValueError as e:
 202:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=str(e))
 203: 
 204: @router.delete("/nodes/{node_id}")
 205: def delete_user_node(node_id: str, request: Request) -> dict:
 206:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 207:     try:
 208:         msg = grid.delete_node(node_id)
 209:         return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 210:     except ValueError as e:
 211:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=str(e))
 212: 
 213: @router.post("/connect")
 214: def add_user_edge(req: EdgeRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 215:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 216:     try:
 217:         msg = grid.add_user_edge(req.source, req.target)
 218:         return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 219:     except ValueError as e:
 220:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=str(e))
 221: 
 222: @router.post("/cut_edge")
 223: def cut_user_edge(req: EdgeRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 224:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 225:     try:
 226:         msg = grid.cut_user_edge(req.source, req.target)
 227:         return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 228:     except ValueError as e:
 229:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=str(e))
 230: 
 231: @router.post("/fail_node")
 232: def fail_user_node(req: NodeTargetRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 233:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 234:     if req.node_id not in grid.nodes:
 235:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="Node not found.")
 236:     msg = grid.inject_failure(req.node_id)
 237:     return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 238: 
 239: @router.post("/restore_node")
 240: def restore_user_node(req: NodeTargetRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 241:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 242:     if req.node_id not in grid.nodes:
 243:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="Node not found.")
 244:     msg = grid.restore_node(req.node_id)
 245:     return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 246: 
 247: @router.post("/command/add_house")
 248: def add_house_to_pole(req: NodeTargetRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 249:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 250:     if req.node_id not in grid.nodes:
 251:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="Node not found.")
 252:     msg = grid.add_house(req.node_id)
 253:     return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 254: 
 255: @router.get("/ai/suggestions")
 256: def get_ai_suggestions(request: Request) -> dict:
 257:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 258:     return {"suggestions": grid.suggest_tie_lines()}
 259: 
 260: @router.post("/ai/suggest_parent")
 261: def post_suggest_parent(req: PositionRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 262:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 263:     return grid.suggest_best_parent(req.x, req.y)
 264: 
 265: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 266: # POST /event
 267: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 268: 
 269: @router.post("/event")
 270: def trigger_event(req: EventRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 271:     """
 272:     Trigger a grid event.
 273:     type: "failure" | "storm" | "clear_storm" | "demand" | "generation" | "restore"
 274:     """
 275:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 276: 
 277:     if req.type == "failure":
 278:         if not req.node_id:
 279:             raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="node_id required for failure event")
 280:         msg = grid.inject_failure(req.node_id)
 281:         return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 282: 
 283:     elif req.type == "storm":
 284:         msg = grid.trigger_storm()
 285:         return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 286: 
 287:     elif req.type == "clear_storm":
 288:         msg = grid.clear_storm()
 289:         return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 290: 
 291:     elif req.type == "demand":
 292:         amount = req.amount if req.amount is not None else 0.2
 293:         msg = grid.increase_demand(amount)
 294:         return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 295: 
 296:     elif req.type == "generation":
 297:         amount = req.amount if req.amount is not None else 0.3
 298:         msg = grid.increase_generation(amount)
 299:         return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 300: 
 301:     elif req.type == "restore":
 302:         if not req.node_id:
 303:             raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="node_id required for restore event")
 304:         msg = grid.restore_node(req.node_id)
 305:         return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 306: 
 307:     else:
 308:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=f"Unknown event type: {req.type}")
 309: 
 310: 
 311: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 312: # GET /predict
 313: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 314: 
 315: @router.get("/predict")
 316: def predict_demand(request: Request, node_id: str = "S0") -> dict:
 317:     """Run LSTM forecasting for a given node."""
 318:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 319:     forecaster: DemandForecaster = get_forecaster(request)
 320:     sequence = grid.get_lstm_input(node_id)
 321:     predicted = forecaster.predict(sequence)
 322:     return {
 323:         "node_id": node_id,
 324:         "predicted_load": round(float(predicted), 4),  # type: ignore
 325:         "sequence_length": len(sequence),
 326:     }
 327: 
 328: 
 329: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 330: # POST /action
 331: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 332: 
 333: @router.post("/action")
 334: def force_action(req: ActionRequest, request: Request) -> dict:
 335:     """Force a specific RL action (0–4)."""
 336:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 337:     scada: ScadaControlCenter = get_scada(request)
 338: 
 339:     if req.action_id < 0 or req.action_id >= N_ACTIONS:
 340:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=f"action_id must be 0–{N_ACTIONS - 1}")
 341: 
 342:     state = grid.get_state()
 343:     action = ACTIONS[req.action_id]
 344:     result = _apply_action(action["name"], state, grid, scada)
 345: 
 346:     return {
 347:         "action": action,
 348:         "result": result,
 349:         "grid": grid.get_state(),
 350:     }
 351: 
 352: 
 353: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 354: # GET /fault_analysis
 355: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 356: 
 357: @router.get("/fault_analysis")
 358: def fault_analysis(request: Request) -> dict:
 359:     """
 360:     Run the AI Fault Detector across all live nodes.
 361:     Returns per-node anomaly scores, fault types, and system health.
 362:     """
 363:     grid: SmartGrid     = get_grid(request)
 364:     detector: FaultDetector = get_fault_detector(request)
 365:     return detector.analyse(grid.nodes)
 366: 
 367: 
 368: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 369: # GET /islanding_analysis
 370: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 371: 
 372: @router.get("/islanding_analysis")
 373: def islanding_analysis(request: Request) -> dict:
 374:     """
 375:     Analyze potential microgrid formation for resilience.
 376:     Returns viable island configurations around healthy generators.
 377:     """
 378:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 379:     failed_nodes = [nid for nid, node in grid.nodes.items() if node.failed]
 380:     return grid.predictive_islanding(failed_nodes)
 381: 
 382: 
 383: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 384: # POST /reset
 385: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 386: 
 387: @router.post("/reset")
 388: def reset_grid(request: Request) -> dict:  # type: ignore[no-redef]
 389:     """Reset the grid to its initial state."""
 390:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 391:     msg = grid.reset()
 392:     return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}
 393: 
 394: 
 395: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 396: # POST /random_fault
 397: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 398: 
 399: @router.post("/random_fault")
 400: def random_fault(request: Request) -> dict:
 401:     """Inject a random failure on a random healthy pole node."""
 402:     grid: SmartGrid = get_grid(request)
 403:     msg = grid.random_failure()
 404:     return {"message": msg, "grid": grid.get_state()}

   1: import sys
   2: sys.path.append('c:/Users/ELCOT/Music/TNWISE/simulation/backend')
   3: from simulation.grid import SmartGrid
   4: from simulation.ems import EnergyManagementSystem
   5: from simulation.scada import ScadaControlCenter
   6: 
   7: grid = SmartGrid()
   8: ems = EnergyManagementSystem()
   9: scada = ScadaControlCenter()
  10: 
  11: print("Initial cycle...")
  12: grid.step()
  13: ems.run(grid)
  14: 
  15: print("\nFailing LA1_2...")
  16: # Use inject_failure() which automatically cuts edges + marks downstream isolated
  17: if "LA1_2" in grid.nodes:
  18:     grid.inject_failure("LA1_2")
  19: else:
  20:     print("Node LA1_2 not found - trying a random pole...")
  21:     grid.random_failure()
  22: 
  23: grid.step()
  24: ems.run(grid)
  25: 
  26: # scada flisr
  27: scada_report = scada.execute_control_loop(grid, ems)
  28: flisr_log = scada_report.get("flisr_log", [])
  29: if flisr_log:
  30:     print("SCADA FLISR log:")
  31:     for entry in flisr_log:
  32:         print(f"  [{entry['step']}] {entry['detail']}")
  33: 
  34: print("\nIsolated nodes:")
  35: for nid, n in grid.nodes.items():
  36:     if n.isolated:
  37:         print(f"{nid} (failed: {n.failed})")

================================================================================
FILE: backend\main.py
================================================================================
   1: """
   2: main.py - FastAPI application entry point.
   3: 
   4: Uses the FastAPI lifespan context manager to initialise singletons and
   5: store them in app.state, making them accessible via dependency injection
   6: in routes (no mutable module-level globals).
   7: 
   8: Run with:
   9:   python main.py
  10:   OR
  11:   uvicorn main:app --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8000
  12: """
  13: 
  14: from __future__ import annotations
  15: 
  16: import sys
  17: import os
  18: from contextlib import asynccontextmanager
  19: 
  20: # Ensure backend root is on the Python path so relative imports resolve
  21: sys.path.insert(0, os.path.dirname(__file__))
  22: 
  23: from fastapi import FastAPI  # type: ignore
  24: from fastapi.middleware.cors import CORSMiddleware  # type: ignore
  25: 
  26: from simulation.grid import SmartGrid  # type: ignore
  27: from simulation.scada import ScadaControlCenter  # type: ignore
  28: from simulation.ems import EnergyManagementSystem  # type: ignore
  29: from api.routes import router  # type: ignore
  30: 
  31: 
  32: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  33: # Lifespan - initialise once, store in app.state
  34: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  35: 
  36: @asynccontextmanager
  37: async def lifespan(app: FastAPI):
  38:     """Startup: build singletons. Shutdown: nothing to clean up."""
  39:     print("=" * 60)
  40:     print("  AI Self-Healing Smart Grid - Backend Starting Up")
  41:     print("=" * 60)
  42: 
  43:     print("\n[1/3] Initialising Structural Level (Physical Grid)...")
  44:     app.state.grid = SmartGrid()
  45:     g: SmartGrid = app.state.grid
  46:     print(f"      Grid created: {len(g.nodes)} nodes, "
  47:           f"{g.graph.number_of_edges()} edges")
  48: 
  49:     print("\n[2/3] Booting Energy Management System (EMS Layer)...")
  50:     app.state.ems = EnergyManagementSystem()
  51:     print("      EMS ready - absorption ratio: 50 %, partial control mode")
  52: 
  53:     print("\n[3/3] Booting SCADA Control Center (AI Layer)...")
  54:     app.state.scada = ScadaControlCenter()
  55:     app.state.scada.warmup_ai(g)  # Pre-train RL agent on grid bounds
  56: 
  57:     print("\n[OK] All systems ready.\n")
  58:     print("=" * 60)
  59: 
  60:     yield   # application runs here
  61: 
  62:     # Teardown (nothing required)
  63: 
  64: 
  65: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  66: # FastAPI App
  67: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  68: 
  69: app = FastAPI(
  70:     title="AI Self-Healing Smart Grid SCADA API",
  71:     description=(
  72:         "Real-time smart grid architecture with a separated SCADA Control Center "
  73:         "managing fault detection and multi-agent demand response."
  74:     ),
  75:     version="2.0.0",
  76:     lifespan=lifespan,
  77: )
  78: 
  79: # CORS - allow React dev server and any local origin
  80: app.add_middleware(
  81:     CORSMiddleware,
  82:     allow_origins=["*"],
  83:     allow_credentials=True,
  84:     allow_methods=["*"],
  85:     allow_headers=["*"],
  86: )
  87: 
  88: app.include_router(router)
  89: 
  90: 
  91: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  92: # Main entry point
  93: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  94: 
  95: if __name__ == "__main__":
  96:     import uvicorn  # type: ignore
  97:     uvicorn.run(
  98:         "main:app",
  99:         host="0.0.0.0",
 100:         port=8000,
 101:         reload=False,
 102:         log_level="info",
 103:     )

================================================================================
FILE: backend\models\fault_detector.py
================================================================================
   1: """
   2: fault_detector.py — AI-based fault detection for the Smart Grid.
   3: 
   4: Architecture:
   5:   - Anomaly Scorer : computes a per-node fault score from voltage, frequency,
   6:                      load, and generation using physics thresholds.
   7:   - ANN Classifier : lightweight 3-layer MLP trained on synthetic fault
   8:                      patterns to classify the fault type.
   9: 
  10: Output per node:
  11:   - fault_score   : 0.0 – 1.0  (anomaly severity)
  12:   - fault_type    : "overload" | "undervoltage" | "frequency_deviation" |
  13:                     "generation_loss" | "normal"
  14:   - is_fault      : bool (score > 0.55)
  15: 
  16: No GPU required — runs on CPU in < 1 ms per call.
  17: """
  18: 
  19: import math
  20: import random
  21: import numpy as np          # type: ignore
  22: import torch                # type: ignore
  23: import torch.nn as nn       # type: ignore
  24: 
  25: 
  26: # ── Fault class labels ────────────────────────────────────────────────
  27: FAULT_TYPES = ["normal", "overload", "undervoltage", "frequency_deviation", "generation_loss"]
  28: FAULT_THRESHOLD = 0.55   # score above this → fault declared
  29: 
  30: 
  31: # ── ANN Classifier ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  32: 
  33: class FaultClassifierANN(nn.Module):
  34:     """
  35:     3-layer MLP.
  36:     Input  : 5 features [voltage, frequency_norm, load, generation, stress]
  37:     Output : 5 class logits (fault types)
  38:     """
  39:     def __init__(self):
  40:         super().__init__()
  41:         self.net = nn.Sequential(
  42:             nn.Linear(5, 32),
  43:             nn.ReLU(),
  44:             nn.Linear(32, 16),
  45:             nn.ReLU(),
  46:             nn.Linear(16, len(FAULT_TYPES)),
  47:         )
  48: 
  49:     def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
  50:         return self.net(x)
  51: 
  52: 
  53: # ── Synthetic Training Data ───────────────────────────────────────────
  54: 
  55: def _generate_fault_data(n: int = 800):
  56:     """
  57:     Generate labelled synthetic fault samples.
  58:     Each sample: [voltage, freq_norm, load, generation, stress] → label
  59:     """
  60:     X, y = [], []
  61:     rng = random.Random(99)
  62: 
  63:     for _ in range(n):
  64:         label = rng.randint(0, len(FAULT_TYPES) - 1)
  65:         fault = FAULT_TYPES[label]
  66: 
  67:         if fault == "normal":
  68:             v   = rng.uniform(0.97, 1.03)
  69:             f   = rng.uniform(49.8, 50.2) / 50.0
  70:             ld  = rng.uniform(0.2, 0.7)
  71:             gen = rng.uniform(0.3, 0.9)
  72:             st  = rng.uniform(0.0, 0.15)
  73:         elif fault == "overload":
  74:             v   = rng.uniform(0.88, 0.96)
  75:             f   = rng.uniform(49.0, 49.7) / 50.0
  76:             ld  = rng.uniform(1.4, 2.0)
  77:             gen = rng.uniform(0.2, 0.6)
  78:             st  = rng.uniform(0.6, 1.0)
  79:         elif fault == "undervoltage":
  80:             v   = rng.uniform(0.80, 0.91)
  81:             f   = rng.uniform(49.2, 50.1) / 50.0
  82:             ld  = rng.uniform(0.5, 1.2)
  83:             gen = rng.uniform(0.1, 0.4)
  84:             st  = rng.uniform(0.5, 0.9)
  85:         elif fault == "frequency_deviation":
  86:             v   = rng.uniform(0.93, 1.05)
  87:             f   = rng.uniform(48.0, 49.3) / 50.0   # or 50.7-52
  88:             f   = f if rng.random() > 0.5 else rng.uniform(50.7, 52.0) / 50.0
  89:             ld  = rng.uniform(0.3, 1.0)
  90:             gen = rng.uniform(0.2, 0.8)
  91:             st  = rng.uniform(0.4, 0.85)
  92:         else:  # generation_loss
  93:             v   = rng.uniform(0.85, 0.97)
  94:             f   = rng.uniform(49.0, 49.8) / 50.0
  95:             ld  = rng.uniform(0.4, 1.0)
  96:             gen = rng.uniform(0.0, 0.15)
  97:             st  = rng.uniform(0.45, 0.9)
  98: 
  99:         X.append([v, f, ld, gen, st])
 100:         y.append(label)
 101: 
 102:     return (np.array(X, dtype=np.float32),
 103:             np.array(y, dtype=np.int64))
 104: 
 105: 
 106: # ── High-level Manager ────────────────────────────────────────────────
 107: 
 108: class FaultDetector:
 109:     """
 110:     Wraps anomaly scoring + ANN fault classification.
 111: 
 112:     Usage in API:
 113:         result = detector.analyse(grid.nodes)
 114:         # result = {
 115:         #   "alerts": [...],           # list of fault events
 116:         #   "node_scores": {...},      # per-node score dict
 117:         #   "system_health": 0.0-1.0,
 118:         # }
 119:     """
 120: 
 121:     def __init__(self):
 122:         self.model = FaultClassifierANN()
 123:         self._train()
 124:         self.model.eval()
 125: 
 126:     def _train(self):
 127:         print("[FaultDetector] Training ANN classifier on synthetic fault data...")
 128:         X, y = _generate_fault_data(n=1000)
 129:         X_t  = torch.tensor(X)
 130:         y_t  = torch.tensor(y)
 131: 
 132:         opt  = torch.optim.Adam(self.model.parameters(), lr=1e-3)
 133:         loss_fn = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()
 134: 
 135:         self.model.train()
 136:         for _ in range(80):
 137:             opt.zero_grad()
 138:             loss = loss_fn(self.model(X_t), y_t)
 139:             loss.backward()
 140:             opt.step()
 141: 
 142:         print(f"[FaultDetector] ANN trained. Final loss: {loss.item():.4f}")
 143: 
 144:     # ── Per-node anomaly score (physics thresholds) ───────────────────
 145:     @staticmethod
 146:     def _anomaly_score(node) -> float:
 147:         """
 148:         3-component score:
 149:           voltage deviation  (nominal = 1.0, dead-band ±0.05)
 150:           frequency deviation (nominal = 50, dead-band ±0.3 Hz)
 151:           load-generation imbalance ratio
 152:         """
 153:         v_dev = max(0.0, abs(node.voltage - 1.0) - 0.05) / 0.15
 154:         f_dev = max(0.0, abs(node.frequency - 50.0) - 0.3) / 2.0
 155:         if node.generation > 0.01:
 156:             imb  = max(0.0, (node.load - node.generation) / max(node.load, 0.01))
 157:         else:
 158:             imb  = 1.0 if node.load > 0.1 else 0.0
 159: 
 160:         score = (0.35 * v_dev + 0.30 * f_dev + 0.35 * imb)
 161:         return float(min(1.0, score))
 162: 
 163:     # ── ANN fault-type classification ────────────────────────────────
 164:     def _classify(self, node) -> str:
 165:         feat = torch.tensor([[
 166:             node.voltage,
 167:             node.frequency / 50.0,
 168:             node.load,
 169:             node.generation,
 170:             node.stress_level,
 171:         ]], dtype=torch.float32)
 172:         with torch.no_grad():
 173:             logits = self.model(feat)
 174:             idx    = int(torch.argmax(logits, dim=1).item())
 175:         return FAULT_TYPES[idx]
 176: 
 177:     # ── Public API ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 178:     def analyse(self, grid_nodes: dict) -> dict:
 179:         """
 180:         Analyse all grid nodes and return structured fault report.
 181: 
 182:         Args:
 183:             grid_nodes: dict of node_id -> GridNode (live node objects)
 184: 
 185:         Returns:
 186:             {
 187:               "alerts":        list of alert dicts for faulted nodes,
 188:               "node_scores":   {node_id: score},
 189:               "system_health": float 0-1,
 190:             }
 191:         """
 192:         alerts      = []
 193:         node_scores = {}
 194: 
 195:         for nid, node in grid_nodes.items():
 196:             # ── HARDWARE FAILURE: node is failed (physical fault) ─────
 197:             if node.failed:
 198:                 node_scores[nid] = 1.0
 199:                 alerts.append({
 200:                     "node_id":    nid,
 201:                     "fault_type": "hard_failure",
 202:                     "score":      1.0,
 203:                     "severity":   "CRITICAL",
 204:                     "message":    f"Node {nid} is offline (hardware failure).",
 205:                 })
 206:                 continue
 207: 
 208:             # ── DE-ENERGIZED: isolated but healthy ─────────────────────
 209:             # This is NOT the same as a hardware fault.
 210:             # The node is physically healthy but cut off pending FLISR restoration.
 211:             # Score = 0.4 (elevated but not critical), severity = MEDIUM
 212:             if node.isolated:
 213:                 node_scores[nid] = 0.4
 214:                 alerts.append({
 215:                     "node_id":    nid,
 216:                     "fault_type": "de_energized",
 217:                     "score":      0.4,
 218:                     "severity":   "MEDIUM",
 219:                     "message":    f"{nid}: De-energized (isolated by sectionalization — awaiting FLISR).",
 220:                 })
 221:                 continue
 222: 
 223:             score      = self._anomaly_score(node)
 224:             fault_type = self._classify(node) if score > 0.25 else "normal"
 225:             node_scores[nid] = round(score, 4)
 226: 
 227:             if score >= FAULT_THRESHOLD:
 228:                 severity = "HIGH" if score >= 0.75 else "MEDIUM"
 229:                 alerts.append({
 230:                     "node_id":    nid,
 231:                     "fault_type": fault_type,
 232:                     "score":      round(score, 4),
 233:                     "severity":   severity,
 234:                     "message":    _alert_msg(nid, fault_type, score),
 235:                 })
 236: 
 237:         # System health = 1 - mean(scores)
 238:         if node_scores:
 239:             system_health = float(max(0.0, 1.0 - sum(node_scores.values()) / len(node_scores)))
 240:         else:
 241:             system_health = 1.0
 242: 
 243:         # Sort by severity
 244:         alerts.sort(key=lambda a: -a["score"])
 245: 
 246:         return {
 247:             "alerts":        alerts[:10],    # top-10 worst
 248:             "node_scores":   node_scores,
 249:             "system_health": round(system_health, 4),
 250:             "fault_count":   len(alerts),
 251:         }
 252: 
 253: 
 254: def _alert_msg(nid: str, fault_type: str, score: float) -> str:
 255:     msgs = {
 256:         "overload":            f"⚠️ {nid}: Overload detected (score {score:.2f}) — demand exceeds capacity.",
 257:         "undervoltage":        f"⚡ {nid}: Undervoltage (score {score:.2f}) — voltage below safe threshold.",
 258:         "frequency_deviation": f"📉 {nid}: Frequency deviation (score {score:.2f}) — grid instability.",
 259:         "generation_loss":     f"🔋 {nid}: Generation loss (score {score:.2f}) — source failure.",
 260:         "normal":              f"✅ {nid}: Anomaly detected (score {score:.2f}) — monitor closely.",
 261:     }
 262:     return msgs.get(fault_type, f"⚠ {nid} anomaly (score {score:.2f})")

================================================================================
FILE: backend\models\lstm_model.py
================================================================================
   1: """
   2: lstm_model.py — Lightweight LSTM for demand forecasting.
   3: 
   4: Architecture:
   5:   Input:  sequence of (load, generation, weather) at 10 timesteps → shape (batch, 10, 3)
   6:   LSTM:   2 layers, hidden_size=32
   7:   Output: predicted next-step demand (scalar)
   8: 
   9: Training:
  10:   Synthetic dataset is generated once at startup (500 samples).
  11:   No GPU required — runs on CPU in <2 seconds.
  12: """
  13: 
  14: import numpy as np  # type: ignore
  15: import torch  # type: ignore
  16: import torch.nn as nn  # type: ignore
  17: from sklearn.preprocessing import MinMaxScaler  # type: ignore
  18: 
  19: 
  20: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  21: # Model Definition
  22: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  23: 
  24: class LSTMForecaster(nn.Module):
  25:     """
  26:     2-layer LSTM followed by a fully-connected head predicting next demand.
  27:     """
  28: 
  29:     def __init__(self, input_size: int = 3, hidden_size: int = 32,
  30:                  num_layers: int = 2, output_size: int = 1):
  31:         super().__init__()
  32:         self.hidden_size = hidden_size
  33:         self.num_layers = num_layers
  34: 
  35:         self.lstm = nn.LSTM(
  36:             input_size=input_size,
  37:             hidden_size=hidden_size,
  38:             num_layers=num_layers,
  39:             batch_first=True,
  40:             dropout=0.1,
  41:         )
  42:         self.fc = nn.Sequential(
  43:             nn.Linear(hidden_size, 16),
  44:             nn.ReLU(),
  45:             nn.Linear(16, output_size),
  46:         )
  47: 
  48:     def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
  49:         # x: (batch, seq_len, input_size)
  50:         h0 = torch.zeros(self.num_layers, x.size(0), self.hidden_size)
  51:         c0 = torch.zeros(self.num_layers, x.size(0), self.hidden_size)
  52:         out, _ = self.lstm(x, (h0, c0))
  53:         # Take only the last timestep's hidden state
  54:         return self.fc(out[:, -1, :])
  55: 
  56: 
  57: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  58: # Dataset Generation
  59: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  60: 
  61: def generate_synthetic_data(n_samples: int = 600, seq_len: int = 10):
  62:     """
  63:     Generate synthetic grid time-series data.
  64: 
  65:     Simulates a day-night load cycle with random noise and occasional spikes.
  66:     Returns (X, y) where:
  67:       X: (n_samples, seq_len, 3)  — [load, generation, weather]
  68:       y: (n_samples,)             — next-step load
  69:     """
  70:     np.random.seed(42)
  71:     t = np.linspace(0, 4 * np.pi, n_samples + seq_len)
  72: 
  73:     # Day-night load cycle
  74:     base_load = 0.5 + 0.3 * np.sin(t) + 0.1 * np.random.randn(len(t))
  75:     base_load = np.clip(base_load, 0.1, 1.5)
  76: 
  77:     # Generation follows solar pattern (peaks at midday)
  78:     generation = 0.6 + 0.25 * np.cos(t + np.pi / 4) + 0.05 * np.random.randn(len(t))
  79:     generation = np.clip(generation, 0.05, 1.2)
  80: 
  81:     # Weather proxy: random storms
  82:     weather = np.zeros(len(t))
  83:     storm_starts = np.random.randint(0, len(t) - 20, 5)
  84:     for s in storm_starts:
  85:         weather[s:s + 20] = np.random.uniform(0.6, 1.0)
  86: 
  87:     X_list, y_list = [], []
  88:     for i in range(n_samples):
  89:         window = np.stack([
  90:             base_load[i:i + seq_len],
  91:             generation[i:i + seq_len],
  92:             weather[i:i + seq_len],
  93:         ], axis=1)
  94:         X_list.append(window)
  95:         y_list.append(base_load[i + seq_len])
  96: 
  97:     X = np.array(X_list, dtype=np.float32)
  98:     y = np.array(y_list, dtype=np.float32)
  99:     return X, y
 100: 
 101: 
 102: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 103: # Training Helper
 104: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 105: 
 106: def train_lstm(model: LSTMForecaster, X: np.ndarray, y: np.ndarray,
 107:                epochs: int = 30, lr: float = 1e-3) -> list:
 108:     """
 109:     Train the LSTM on synthetic data. Returns loss history.
 110:     Designed to complete in <5 seconds on CPU.
 111:     """
 112:     model.train()
 113:     optimizer = torch.optim.Adam(model.parameters(), lr=lr)
 114:     criterion = nn.MSELoss()
 115: 
 116:     X_t = torch.tensor(X)
 117:     y_t = torch.tensor(y).unsqueeze(1)
 118: 
 119:     losses = []
 120:     for epoch in range(epochs):
 121:         optimizer.zero_grad()
 122:         pred = model(X_t)  # type: ignore
 123:         loss = criterion(pred, y_t)
 124:         loss.backward()
 125:         optimizer.step()
 126:         losses.append(loss.item())
 127: 
 128:     return losses
 129: 
 130: 
 131: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 132: # Top-Level Manager
 133: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 134: 
 135: class DemandForecaster:
 136:     """
 137:     High-level wrapper used by the API.
 138:     - Generates synthetic training data at startup
 139:     - Pre-trains the LSTM (fast, CPU-only)
 140:     - Provides predict() for the /predict endpoint
 141:     """
 142: 
 143:     SEQ_LEN = 10
 144: 
 145:     def __init__(self):
 146:         self.model = LSTMForecaster()
 147:         self.scaler = MinMaxScaler()
 148:         self._pretrain()
 149: 
 150:     def _pretrain(self):
 151:         """Train the LSTM on synthetic data at startup."""
 152:         print("[LSTM] Generating synthetic dataset...")
 153:         X, y = generate_synthetic_data(n_samples=500, seq_len=self.SEQ_LEN)
 154: 
 155:         # Fit scaler on flattened features
 156:         flat = X.reshape(-1, 3)
 157:         self.scaler.fit(flat)
 158: 
 159:         # Normalise
 160:         X_norm = np.array([
 161:             self.scaler.transform(x) for x in X
 162:         ], dtype=np.float32)
 163: 
 164:         print("[LSTM] Training on CPU (30 epochs)...")
 165:         losses = train_lstm(self.model, X_norm, y, epochs=30)
 166:         print(f"[LSTM] Training complete. Final loss: {losses[-1]:.6f}")
 167:         self.model.eval()
 168: 
 169:     def predict(self, sequence: list) -> float:
 170:         """
 171:         Predict the next demand given a list of 10 [load, gen, weather] triples.
 172: 
 173:         Args:
 174:             sequence: list of 10 lists, each [load, generation, weather]
 175:         Returns:
 176:             Predicted next load (float, unnormalised)
 177:         """
 178:         if len(sequence) < self.SEQ_LEN:
 179:             sequence = [[0.5, 0.5, 0.0]] * (self.SEQ_LEN - len(sequence)) + sequence
 180: 
 181:         seq_arr = np.array(sequence[-self.SEQ_LEN:], dtype=np.float32)  # type: ignore
 182:         seq_norm = self.scaler.transform(seq_arr)
 183:         x_t = torch.tensor(seq_norm).unsqueeze(0)  # (1, 10, 3)
 184: 
 185:         with torch.no_grad():
 186:             pred = self.model(x_t).item()  # type: ignore
 187: 
 188:         # Clamp to reasonable demand range
 189:         return float(np.clip(pred, 0.05, 2.0))

================================================================================
FILE: backend\models\rl_agent.py
================================================================================
   1: """
   2: rl_agent.py — DQN Reinforcement Learning agent for smart grid control.
   3: 
   4: State  (per node): [voltage, frequency/50, load, generation, stress] × 8 nodes = 40-dim
   5: Actions (5 discrete):
   6:   0 → Increase generation on all substations
   7:   1 → Use battery storage (highest-deficit node)
   8:   2 → Use supercapacitor (largest spike node)
   9:   3 → Shift load (reduce 10% on house nodes)
  10:   4 → Reroute energy (activate cross-links, trigger multi-agent share)
  11: 
  12: Reward:
  13:   +2   per node close to nominal voltage (|v−1| < 0.05)
  14:   +1   per node close to nominal frequency (|f−50| < 0.2)
  15:   -5   per failed/isolated node
  16:   -1   per node with stress > 0.7
  17:   -0.1 × total_energy_loss (cost proxy)
  18: 
  19: DQN details:
  20:   - 2-hidden-layer MLP (64→64)
  21:   - Replay buffer (capacity 2000)
  22:   - ε-greedy exploration (ε decays 1.0 → 0.05)
  23:   - Target network updated every 20 steps
  24:   - Warms up on 100 random experience samples at startup
  25: """
  26: 
  27: from __future__ import annotations
  28: 
  29: import random
  30: import math
  31: from collections import deque
  32: from typing import Optional
  33: 
  34: import numpy as np  # type: ignore
  35: import torch  # type: ignore
  36: import torch.nn as nn  # type: ignore
  37: import torch.optim as optim  # type: ignore
  38: 
  39: 
  40: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  41: # Action Catalogue
  42: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  43: 
  44: ACTIONS = [
  45:     {
  46:         "id": 0,
  47:         "name": "increase_generation",
  48:         "label": "⚡ Boosting generation on substations",
  49:         "color": "green",
  50:     },
  51:     {
  52:         "id": 1,
  53:         "name": "use_battery",
  54:         "label": "🔋 Drawing from battery storage",
  55:         "color": "blue",
  56:     },
  57:     {
  58:         "id": 2,
  59:         "name": "use_supercapacitor",
  60:         "label": "⚡ Discharging supercapacitor (spike suppression)",
  61:         "color": "cyan",
  62:     },
  63:     {
  64:         "id": 3,
  65:         "name": "shift_load",
  66:         "label": "📊 Deferring non-critical loads",
  67:         "color": "yellow",
  68:     },
  69:     {
  70:         "id": 4,
  71:         "name": "reroute_energy",
  72:         "label": "🔀 Rerouting energy via alternate paths",
  73:         "color": "purple",
  74:     },
  75: ]
  76: 
  77: N_ACTIONS = len(ACTIONS)
  78: STATE_DIM = 52   # (3 Gen + 6 Sub) × 5 features + 7 global features
  79: 
  80: 
  81: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  82: # Neural Network Q-function
  83: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  84: 
  85: class DQNetwork(nn.Module):
  86:     """Simple MLP approximating Q(s, a) for all actions simultaneously."""
  87: 
  88:     def __init__(self, state_dim: int = STATE_DIM, n_actions: int = N_ACTIONS):
  89:         super().__init__()
  90:         self.net = nn.Sequential(
  91:             nn.Linear(state_dim, 64),
  92:             nn.ReLU(),
  93:             nn.Linear(64, 64),
  94:             nn.ReLU(),
  95:             nn.Linear(64, n_actions),
  96:         )
  97: 
  98:     def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
  99:         return self.net(x)
 100: 
 101: 
 102: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 103: # Replay Buffer
 104: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 105: 
 106: class ReplayBuffer:
 107:     def __init__(self, capacity: int = 2000):
 108:         self.buf = deque(maxlen=capacity)
 109: 
 110:     def push(self, state, action, reward, next_state, done):
 111:         self.buf.append((state, action, reward, next_state, done))
 112: 
 113:     def sample(self, batch_size: int):
 114:         batch = random.sample(self.buf, batch_size)
 115:         s, a, r, ns, d = zip(*batch)
 116:         return (
 117:             torch.tensor(np.array(s), dtype=torch.float32),
 118:             torch.tensor(a, dtype=torch.long),
 119:             torch.tensor(r, dtype=torch.float32),
 120:             torch.tensor(np.array(ns), dtype=torch.float32),
 121:             torch.tensor(d, dtype=torch.float32),
 122:         )
 123: 
 124:     def __len__(self):
 125:         return len(self.buf)
 126: 
 127: 
 128: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 129: # DQN Agent
 130: # -----------------------------------------------------------------------
 131: 
 132: class DQNAgent:
 133:     """
 134:     Deep Q-Network agent for smart grid control.
 135:     Designed for CPU-only, fast iteration — suitable for hackathon demo.
 136:     """
 137: 
 138:     GAMMA = 0.95
 139:     LR = 1e-3
 140:     BATCH_SIZE = 32
 141:     EPSILON_START = 1.0
 142:     EPSILON_END = 0.05
 143:     EPSILON_DECAY = 200   # steps to decay ε
 144:     TARGET_UPDATE = 20    # steps between target network sync
 145: 
 146:     def __init__(self):
 147:         self.policy_net = DQNetwork()
 148:         self.target_net = DQNetwork()
 149:         self.target_net.load_state_dict(self.policy_net.state_dict())
 150:         self.target_net.eval()
 151: 
 152:         self.optimizer = optim.Adam(self.policy_net.parameters(), lr=self.LR)
 153:         self.buffer = ReplayBuffer()
 154:         self.criterion = nn.SmoothL1Loss()   # Huber loss
 155: 
 156:         self.steps_done = 0
 157:         self.epsilon = self.EPSILON_START
 158:         self._last_action_id = 0
 159:         self._last_reasoning = ""
 160: 
 161:         # Warm up is now called externally via smart_warmup(grid)
 162: 
 163:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 164:     # Exploration schedule
 165:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 166: 
 167:     def _get_epsilon(self) -> float:
 168:         """Exponential ε decay."""
 169:         eps = self.EPSILON_END + (self.EPSILON_START - self.EPSILON_END) * \
 170:               math.exp(-self.steps_done / self.EPSILON_DECAY)
 171:         return eps
 172: 
 173:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 174:     # Rule-Guided Warm-Up
 175:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 176: 
 177:     def smart_warmup(self, grid, scada_instance=None):
 178:         """
 179:         Rule-guided warmup to populate replay buffer with intentional experiences.
 180:         Learns from an 'expert policy' to kickstart DQN stability.
 181:         """
 182:         print("[DQN] Warming up replay buffer via expert imitation...")
 183: 
 184:         for _ in range(150):
 185:             state = grid.get_rl_state()
 186:             state_dict = grid.get_state()
 187: 
 188:             sys_info = state_dict.get("system", {})
 189:             nodes = state_dict.get("nodes", {})
 190:             balance = sys_info.get("balance", 0.0)
 191:             num_failed = sum(1 for n in nodes.values() if n.get("failed"))
 192:             num_isolated = sum(1 for n in nodes.values() if n.get("isolated"))
 193:             has_spike = any(n.get("load", 0) > 1.2 for n in nodes.values())
 194: 
 195:             # Simple rule-based expert
 196:             if num_failed > 0 or num_isolated > 0:
 197:                 action_id = 4 # reroute
 198:             elif has_spike:
 199:                 action_id = 2 # supercapacitor
 200:             elif balance < -0.3:
 201:                 action_id = 0 # increase gen
 202:             elif balance < -0.1:
 203:                 action_id = 1 # battery
 204:             else:
 205:                 action_id = 3 # drop load
 206: 
 207:             action_name = str(ACTIONS[action_id]["name"])
 208: 
 209:             # Apply and step
 210:             if scada_instance:
 211:                 scada_instance._dispatch_control_signal(action_name, state_dict, grid)
 212:             grid.step()
 213: 
 214:             next_state_dict = grid.get_state()
 215:             next_state = grid.get_rl_state()
 216:             reward = self.compute_reward(next_state_dict, action_name)
 217: 
 218:             s = np.array(state, dtype=np.float32)
 219:             ns = np.array(next_state, dtype=np.float32)
 220:             self.buffer.push(s, action_id, reward, ns, False)
 221: 
 222:             # Inject random failure to teach recovery (disabled for clean startup)
 223:             # if random.random() < 0.02:
 224:             #     grid.inject_failure(random.choice(["H0", "H1", "H2", "H3", "H4"]))
 225: 
 226:         # Run a batch of training to initialize network
 227:         for _ in range(40):
 228:             self._train_step()
 229: 
 230:         grid.reset()
 231:         grid.heal_all()  # Ensure clean startup state
 232:         print("[DQN] Smart warmup complete.")
 233: 
 234:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 235:     # Action Selection
 236:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 237: 
 238:     def select_action(self, state: list, predicted_load: float = 0.5,
 239:                       grid_state: Optional[dict] = None) -> dict:
 240:         """
 241:         Choose an action given the current state vector and context.
 242:         Builds a human-readable reasoning string explaining the choice.
 243: 
 244:         Returns dict with: action_id, action_name, label, color, reasoning
 245:         """
 246:         state_vec = np.array(state, dtype=np.float32)
 247:         self.epsilon = self._get_epsilon()
 248:         self.steps_done += 1
 249: 
 250:         # Action Masking Logic
 251:         valid_actions = []
 252:         if grid_state:
 253:             sys_info = grid_state.get("system", {})
 254:             nodes = grid_state.get("nodes", {})
 255:             balance = sys_info.get("balance", 0.0)
 256:             failed = any(n.get("failed") for n in nodes.values())
 257:             isolated = any(n.get("isolated") for n in nodes.values())
 258:             spike = any(n.get("load", 0) > 1.2 for n in nodes.values())
 259: 
 260:             if balance < -0.1: valid_actions.extend([0, 1])
 261:             if spike: valid_actions.append(2)
 262:             if failed or isolated: valid_actions.append(4)
 263:             valid_actions.append(3) # Load shift is always an option
 264: 
 265:         if not valid_actions:
 266:             valid_actions = [0, 1, 2, 3, 4]
 267: 
 268:         valid_actions = list(set(valid_actions))
 269: 
 270:         # Action Selection and Confidence
 271:         confidence = 0.0
 272:         with torch.no_grad():
 273:             q_vals = self.policy_net(torch.tensor(state_vec).unsqueeze(0))  # type: ignore
 274:             mask = torch.full((1, N_ACTIONS), float('-inf'))
 275:             for a in valid_actions:
 276:                 mask[0, a] = 0.0
 277: 
 278:             masked_q = q_vals + mask
 279:             best_action = masked_q.argmax(dim=1).item()
 280: 
 281:             # Extract confidence using Softmax over valid actions
 282:             valid_q = q_vals[mask == 0.0]
 283:             if len(valid_q) > 0:
 284:                 probs = torch.nn.functional.softmax(valid_q, dim=0)
 285:                 confidence = probs.max().item()
 286: 
 287:         # Epsilon Greedy Override
 288:         if random.random() < self.epsilon:
 289:             action_id = random.choice(valid_actions)
 290:             confidence = 1.0 / len(valid_actions)  # Low confidence on random jump
 291:         else:
 292:             action_id = best_action
 293: 
 294:         self._last_action_id = action_id
 295:         action = ACTIONS[action_id]
 296: 
 297:         # Build reasoning
 298:         reasoning = self._build_reasoning(action_id, predicted_load, grid_state)
 299:         self._last_reasoning = reasoning
 300: 
 301:         return {
 302:             "action_id": action_id,
 303:             "action_name": action["name"],
 304:             "label": action["label"],
 305:             "color": action["color"],
 306:             "reasoning": reasoning,
 307:             "epsilon": round(float(self.epsilon), 3),  # type: ignore
 308:             "confidence": round(float(confidence), 3),
 309:         }
 310: 
 311:     def _build_reasoning(self, action_id: int, predicted_load: float,
 312:                           grid_state: Optional[dict]) -> str:
 313:         """Generate a human-readable explanation of why this action was chosen."""
 314:         ctx_parts = []
 315: 
 316:         if grid_state:
 317:             sys = grid_state.get("system", {})
 318:             balance = sys.get("balance", 0)
 319:             health = sys.get("health_score", 1.0)
 320:             avg_v = sys.get("avg_voltage", 1.0)
 321:             storm = grid_state.get("storm_active", False)
 322:             failed = [nid for nid, n in grid_state.get("nodes", {}).items() if n.get("failed")]
 323: 
 324:             if storm:
 325:                 ctx_parts.append("🌩️ Storm active — high demand")
 326:             if failed:
 327:                 ctx_parts.append(f"⚠️ Node(s) {failed} are failed")
 328:             if predicted_load > 0.8:
 329:                 ctx_parts.append(f"📈 High demand predicted ({predicted_load:.2f} MW)")
 330:             elif predicted_load < 0.3:
 331:                 ctx_parts.append(f"📉 Low demand predicted ({predicted_load:.2f} MW)")
 332:             if balance < -0.3:
 333:                 ctx_parts.append("🔴 Grid deficit detected")
 334:             elif balance > 0.5:
 335:                 ctx_parts.append("🟢 Grid surplus — stable")
 336:             if health < 0.5:
 337:                 ctx_parts.append(f"🚨 System health low ({health:.0%})")
 338:             if abs(avg_v - 1.0) > 0.08:
 339:                 ctx_parts.append(f"⚡ Voltage deviation ({avg_v:.3f} p.u.)")
 340: 
 341:         context = " | ".join(ctx_parts) if ctx_parts else "Routine monitoring"
 342:         action_label = ACTIONS[action_id]["label"]
 343: 
 344:         return f"{context} → {action_label}"
 345: 
 346:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 347:     # Learning
 348:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 349: 
 350:     def store_experience(self, state: list, action_id: int, reward: float,
 351:                          next_state: list, done: bool = False):
 352:         """Push a transition to the replay buffer and train."""
 353:         s = np.array(state, dtype=np.float32)
 354:         ns = np.array(next_state, dtype=np.float32)
 355:         self.buffer.push(s, action_id, reward, ns, done)
 356: 
 357:         if len(self.buffer) >= self.BATCH_SIZE:
 358:             self._train_step()
 359: 
 360:         # Periodically sync target network
 361:         if self.steps_done % self.TARGET_UPDATE == 0:
 362:             self.target_net.load_state_dict(self.policy_net.state_dict())
 363: 
 364:     def _train_step(self):
 365:         """One gradient-descent step on a random batch from the replay buffer."""
 366:         if len(self.buffer) < self.BATCH_SIZE:
 367:             return
 368: 
 369:         states, actions, rewards, next_states, dones = self.buffer.sample(self.BATCH_SIZE)
 370: 
 371:         # Zero gradients BEFORE forward pass to avoid stale graph references
 372:         self.optimizer.zero_grad()
 373: 
 374:         # Current Q-values for taken actions (fresh forward pass)
 375:         q_values = self.policy_net(states).gather(1, actions.unsqueeze(1)).squeeze(-1)
 376: 
 377:         # Target Q-values (Bellman equation) — fully detached from computation graph
 378:         with torch.no_grad():
 379:             next_q = self.target_net(next_states).max(1)[0]
 380:             targets = (rewards + self.GAMMA * next_q * (1 - dones)).detach()
 381: 
 382:         loss = self.criterion(q_values, targets)
 383:         loss.backward()
 384:         # Gradient clipping for stability
 385:         nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_(self.policy_net.parameters(), 1.0)
 386:         self.optimizer.step()
 387: 
 388:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 389:     # Reward Computation
 390:     # ------------------------------------------------------------------
 391: 
 392:     @staticmethod
 393:     def compute_reward(grid_state: dict, action_name: str = "") -> float:
 394:         """
 395:         Compute a sharp, intentional reward focused on stability, balance, and minimizing failure.
 396:         """
 397:         reward = 0.0
 398:         nodes = grid_state.get("nodes", {})
 399:         system = grid_state.get("system", {})
 400: 
 401:         avg_voltage = system.get("avg_voltage", 1.0)
 402:         avg_freq = system.get("avg_frequency", 50.0)
 403:         balance = system.get("balance", 0.0)
 404:         total_energy_loss = system.get("total_energy_loss", 0.0)
 405: 
 406:         num_failed = sum(1 for n in nodes.values() if n.get("failed"))
 407:         num_isolated = sum(1 for n in nodes.values() if n.get("isolated"))
 408: 
 409:         # Stability (HIGH priority)
 410:         reward += 5.0 * (1.0 - abs(avg_voltage - 1.0) / 0.1)
 411:         reward += 3.0 * (1.0 - abs(avg_freq - 50.0) / 1.5)
 412: 
 413:         # Balance (VERY IMPORTANT)
 414:         reward -= 4.0 * abs(balance)
 415: 
 416:         # Failure penalty (CRITICAL)
 417:         reward -= 10.0 * num_failed
 418:         reward -= 6.0 * num_isolated
 419: 
 420:         # Efficiency
 421:         reward -= 0.2 * total_energy_loss
 422: 
 423:         # Smart behavior conditional bonuses
 424:         if action_name == "use_supercapacitor" and any(n.get("load", 0) > 1.2 for n in nodes.values()):
 425:             reward += 2.0
 426: 
 427:         if action_name == "reroute_energy" and (num_failed > 0 or num_isolated > 0):
 428:             reward += 3.0
 429: 
 430:         return float(reward)
